\sctn{Main program definition} %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

This is the {\prog} program outline:

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{3}\sublabel{NWgff18-APL5-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-APL5-1}}}\moddef{APLOT~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-APL5-1}}}\endmoddef
\LA{}PERL shebang~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-PERC-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Program Info~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ProC-1}}\RA{}
#
# MODULES
#
\LA{}Use Modules~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UseB-1}}\RA{}
#
# CONSTANTS
#
\LA{}Global Constants~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-1}}\RA{}
#
# VARIABLES
#
\LA{}Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}UNDEFINED VARS~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UNDE-1}}\RA{}
#
# MAIN PROGRAM LOOP
#
\LA{}Main Loop~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-Mai9-1}}\RA{}
#
# MAIN FUNCTIONS
#
\LA{}Main Routines~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}\RA{}
#
# GENERAL FUNCTIONS
#
\LA{}Common Routines~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ComF-1}}\RA{}
#
# POSTSCRIPT CODE

\LA{}PostScript CODE Chunks~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-PosM-1}}\RA{}
\nwnotused{APLOT}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{4}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{The main loop}

At the first stage of the new {\prog} implementation, we are going to define a simple main loop that performs a serial process, such in the old {\tt{}GNUawk} version. So that, the program will read the input files and parameters defined by user and perform the plots, finishing the job. Once the new version will be operative, we will try to implement an iterative mode and/or a GUI in {\tt{}perlTK}.  

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{5}\sublabel{NWgff18-Mai9-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-Mai9-1}}}\moddef{Main Loop~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-Mai9-1}}}\endmoddef

  # &set_default_vars;

  %CmdLineVars = ();            # Reseting Command-Line OPTIONS
  &parse_command_line;

  %CustomVars = ();             # Reseting Customization OPTIONS
  &parse_custom_files;
  %gff_data = %aplot_data = (); # Reseting DATA
  &parse_GFF_files;

  &map_vars_data;

  &sort_elements;
  &make_plot;

  $total_time = &timing($T);
  &header("$PROGRAM HAS FINISHED","Timing: $total_time secs");
  
  &close_logfile();
  exit(0);
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{6}\nwdocspar

We force that all the variables must be declared before using them and restrict unsafe constructs with'{\tt{}use\ strict}'. After that we switch on signal trapping.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{7}\sublabel{NWgff18-UseB-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UseB-1}}}\moddef{Use Modules~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UseB-1}}}\endmoddef
use strict;
#
\LA{}Trapping signals~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-TraG-1}}\RA{}
#
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-UseB-2}\\{NWgff18-UseB-3}\\{NWgff18-UseB-4}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{8}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{9}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloG-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-1}}}\moddef{Global Constants~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-1}}}\endmoddef
my ($T,$F) = (1,0); # for 'T'rue and 'F'alse
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-GloG-2}\\{NWgff18-GloG-3}\\{NWgff18-GloG-4}\\{NWgff18-GloG-5}\\{NWgff18-GloG-6}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{10}\nwdocspar

Those are the main variables containing customization parameters and input data from GFF records.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{11}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\endmoddef
my (%DefaultVars,%CmdLineVars,%CustomVars,%gff_data,%aplot_data);
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-GloB-2}\\{NWgff18-GloB-3}\\{NWgff18-GloB-4}\\{NWgff18-GloB-5}\\{NWgff18-GloB-6}\\{NWgff18-GloB-7}\\{NWgff18-GloB-8}\\{NWgff18-GloB-9}\\{NWgff18-GloB-A}\\{NWgff18-GloB-B}\\{NWgff18-GloB-C}\\{NWgff18-GloB-D}\\{NWgff18-GloB-E}\\{NWgff18-GloB-F}\\{NWgff18-GloB-G}\\{NWgff18-GloB-H}\\{NWgff18-GloB-I}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{12}\nwdocspar

Some info about the program itself.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{13}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloG-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-2}}}\moddef{Global Constants~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my ($PROGRAM,$VERSION,$REVISION,$REVISION_DATE,$LAST_UPDATE) = 
   ( 'gff2aplot','v2.0',
     '$Revision: 1.1 $', #'
     '$Date: 2001-08-21 14:54:21 $', #'
     '$Id: gff2aplot.tex,v 1.1 2001-08-21 14:54:21 jabril Exp $', #'
    );
$REVISION =~ s/\\$//og;
$REVISION_DATE =~ s/\\$//og;
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{14} %$

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{15}\sublabel{NWgff18-UNDE-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UNDE-1}}}\moddef{UNDEFINED VARS~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UNDE-1}}}\endmoddef
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{16}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Main function sections}

Main function calls share a similar internal structure: a '{\tt{}header}' reporting which function is running, the '{\tt{}code}' for that function and maybe a '{\tt{}closing\ report}' summarizing what the function did. After each main function definition, you should find those constants, variables and routines being used by that function.  

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{17}\sublabel{NWgff18-MaiD-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}}\moddef{Main Routines~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}}\endmoddef
\LA{}Setting Defaults~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-SetG-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Parsing Command-Line Options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Parsing Custom Files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Sorting Features~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-SorG-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Features Setting~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-FeaG-1}}\RA{}
\LA{}Making PS Figures~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-MakH-1}}\RA{}
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-2}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{18}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Printing Help}

Here is shown the basic outline being diplayed when user choose the '{\tt{}help}' command-line option. The '{\tt{}REQUIRES}' section summarizes those perl modules used in this program by joining all the comments in this document under '{\tt{}\LA{}requires help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{nw@notdef}}\RA{}}' tag. Similar happens to '{\tt{}COMMAND-LINE\ OPTIONS}', in which the single descriptions for each option (that follows each option '{\tt{}Getopts}' definition) are collected by the '{\tt{}\LA{}command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}\RA{}}' tag.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{19}\sublabel{NWgff18-MaiD-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-MaiD-2}}}\moddef{Main Routines~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub prt_help() \{
    open(HELP, "| more") ;
    print HELP <<"+++EndOfHelp+++";
PROGRAM:
                        $PROGRAM - $VERSION

    Converting GFF files for pairwise alignments to PostScript.

USAGE:        $PROGRAM [options] <GFF_files|STDIN>

DESCRIPTION:

    This program draws color-filled alignment plots from GFF
    files for that alignment and two sequences annotations.

REQUIRES:

    \LA{}perl requires help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-perI-1}}\RA{}

ENVIRONMENT VARIABLES:

    \LA{}environment vars help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-envL-1}}\RA{}

COMMAND-LINE OPTIONS:

    \LA{}command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}\RA{}

    \LA{}colors help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-colB-1}}\RA{}

    \LA{}pages help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-pagA-1}}\RA{}

BUGS:    Report any problem to 'jabril\\@imim.es'.

AUTHOR:  $PROGRAM is under GNU-GPL (C) 2000 - Josep F. Abril

+++EndOfHelp+++
    close(HELP);
    exit(1);
\} # prt_help
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{20}%$

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{21}\sublabel{NWgff18-perI-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-perI-1}}}\moddef{perl requires help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-perI-1}}}\endmoddef
$PROGRAM needs the following Perl modules installed in 
your system, we used those available from the standard 
Perl distribution. Those that are not in the standard 
distribution are marked with an '(*)', in such cases 
make sure that you already have downloaded them from 
CPAN (http://www.perl.com/CPAN) and installed.

\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-perI-2}\\{NWgff18-perI-3}\\{NWgff18-perI-4}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-2}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{22}%$

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{23}\sublabel{NWgff18-comH-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}}\moddef{command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}}\endmoddef
A double dash on itself "--" signals end of the options
and start of file names (if present). You can use a single
dash "-" as STDIN placeholder. Available options and a
short description are listed here:

\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-comH-2}\\{NWgff18-comH-3}\\{NWgff18-comH-4}\\{NWgff18-comH-5}\\{NWgff18-comH-6}\\{NWgff18-comH-7}\\{NWgff18-comH-8}\\{NWgff18-comH-9}\\{NWgff18-comH-A}\\{NWgff18-comH-B}\\{NWgff18-comH-C}\\{NWgff18-comH-D}\\{NWgff18-comH-E}\\{NWgff18-comH-F}\\{NWgff18-comH-G}\\{NWgff18-comH-H}\\{NWgff18-comH-I}\\{NWgff18-comH-J}\\{NWgff18-comH-K}\\{NWgff18-comH-L}\\{NWgff18-comH-M}\\{NWgff18-comH-N}\\{NWgff18-comH-O}\\{NWgff18-comH-P}\\{NWgff18-comH-Q}\\{NWgff18-comH-R}\\{NWgff18-comH-S}\\{NWgff18-comH-T}\\{NWgff18-comH-U}\\{NWgff18-comH-V}\\{NWgff18-comH-W}\\{NWgff18-comH-X}\\{NWgff18-comH-Y}\\{NWgff18-comH-Z}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-2}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{24}\nwdocspar

\sctn{Variable Definition and Customization} %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

The functions described in this section process each GFF-record, each custom definition or each command-line options, not only loading the internal variables, also checking for the correctness of the user input in each case.

\subsctn{Setting customization parameters from defaults} 

The main difference from older versions, besides a cleaner hash structure than the GAWK one, is that we include some customization variables at sequence and strand levels. Almost all the variables are described in section~\ref{sec:customvardesc}, page~\pageref{sec:customvardesc}.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{25}\sublabel{NWgff18-SetG-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-SetG-1}}}\moddef{Setting Defaults~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-SetG-1}}}\endmoddef
sub set_default_vars() \{
    %DefaultVars = (
        LAYOUT   => \{           ## '# L #'
            \LA{}default layout vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defQ-1}}\RA{}
        \},                    
        SEQUENCE => \{           ## '# Q #'
            \LA{}default sequence vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defS-1}}\RA{}
        \},                    
        SOURCE   => \{           ## '# S #'
            \LA{}default source vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defQ.2-1}}\RA{}
        \},                    
        STRAND   => \{           ## '# T #'
            \LA{}default strand vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defQ.3-1}}\RA{}
        \},                    
        GROUP    => \{           ## '# G #'
            \LA{}default group vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defP-1}}\RA{}
        \},                    
        FEATURE  => \{           ## '# F #'
            \LA{}default feature vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defR-1}}\RA{}
        \},
    ); # %DefaultVars
    print LOGFILE Dumper(\\%DefaultVars) if ($LogFile && $Debug);
\} # set_default_vars
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{26}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Default customization files}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{27}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-2}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my $Custom_path = $ENV\{GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMPATH\};
my $Custom_file = $ENV\{GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMFILE\};
defined($Custom_path) || ($Custom_path = '.');
defined($Custom_file) || ($Custom_file = '.gff2aplotrc');
$Custom_path =~ s\{/$\}\{\}o; 
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{28}\nwdocspar

We remove any trailing '{\tt{}/}' from '{\tt{}{\char36}Custom{\char95}path}' that user could have introduced to avoid any problem with full custom filenames later.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{29}\sublabel{NWgff18-envL-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-envL-1}}}\moddef{environment vars help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-envL-1}}}\endmoddef
    There are two environmental variables that can be set by 
users to their preferences:
 + You can specify the path where $PROGRAM can find the default
  files with the shell variable \\"GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMPATH\\". Default
  value is the path where you are running $PROGRAM.
 + You can also define the default custom filename you will like
  with the variable \\"GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMFILE\\", program default
  filename for custom file is \\".gff2aplotrc\\".
 + Now $PROGRAM does not need to write any temporary file, 
  so that previous versions default temporary directory path
  variable (\\"GFF2APLOT_TMP\\") is no longer used.
 + Setting those vars in Bourne-shell and C-shell:
   o Using a Bourne-Shell (e.g. bash):
        export GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMPATH=\\"path\\"
        export GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMFILE=\\"file_name\\"
   o Using a C-Shell:
        setenv GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMPATH \\"path\\"
        setenv GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMFILE \\"file_name\\"
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-2}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{30}%$


\subsctn{Setting customization parameters from command-line} 

'{\tt{}GetOptions}' loads command-line options as key-value pairs in the hash variable '{\tt{}{\char37}CmdLineVars}' 
that is reset in '{\tt{}\LA{}Main Loop~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-Mai9-1}}\RA{}}'. Once parsed all the command-line options what remains in '{\tt{}@ARGV}' is just input filenames (which have to be in GFF format), or '{\tt{}STDIN}' if there is none.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{31}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParS-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-1}}}\moddef{Parsing Command-Line Options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-1}}}\endmoddef
sub parse_command_line() \{
    \LA{}looking for STDIN~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-looH-1}}\RA{}

    $SIG\{__WARN__\} = sub \{ &warn('UNKNOWN_CL_OPTION',$T,$_[0]) \};
    GetOptions(
               \LA{}command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}\RA{}
               ) || (&warn('CMD_LINE_ERROR',$T), exit(1));
    $SIG\{__WARN__\} = 'DEFAULT';

    \LA{}open LOGFILE~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-opeC-1}}\RA{}

    &header('',"RUNNING $PROGRAM",'',"User: $USER","Date: $DATE");

    &header("SETTING DEFAULTS");
    %DefaultVars = ();
    &set_default_vars;

    &header("CHECKING COMMAND-LINE OPTIONS");
    @data_files = ();
    &set_input_file($cmdln_stdin);
    @ARGV = (); # ensuring that command-line ARGVs array is empty

    &set_custom_files();

    \LA{}Check command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-CheQ-1}}\RA{}

    &footer("COMMAND-LINE CHECKED");
\} # parse_command_line
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-ParS-2}\\{NWgff18-ParS-3}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{32}\nwdocspar

As the '{\tt{}GetOptions}' function has a problem, in the way we are using here to preserve backwards compatibility, when we want to use a single dash as a way to tell the program that '{\tt{}STDIN}' must be read in the given order (when input filenames are also given and we would load input from a pipe after/before a given file). We show the warnings printed by the program when '{\tt{}--}' is missing or missplaced in the table~\ref{tbl:STDINhandle}.

\begin{table}[!t]
\begin{center}
\begin{small}
\begin{tabular}{|c|}\hline
\begin{minipage}{15cm}
\begin{verbatim}

# CORRECT
> $BIN/gff2aplot -v -T 'Howdy World!' -- - DATA-SAMPLE.gff 
> $BIN/gff2aplot -v -T 'Howdy World!' -- DATA-SAMPLE.gff -

# WRONG???
> $BIN/gff2aplot -v -T 'Howdy World!' DATA-SAMPLE.gff -
> $BIN/gff2aplot -v -T 'Howdy World!' - DATA-SAMPLE.gff
> $BIN/gff2aplot -v -T 'Howdy World!' - -- tests/DATA-SAMPLE.gff

# COMMON MESSAGE when WRONG
### WARNING ### Error trapped while processing command-line:
                substr outside of string at lib/Getopt/Long.pm
                  (autosplit into lib/auto/Getopt/Long/FindOption.al)
                line >NNNNN<
### WARNING ### Error trapped while processing command-line:
                Use of uninitialized value at lib/Getopt/Long.pm
                  (autosplit into lib/auto/Getopt/Long/FindOption.al) 
                line >NNNNN<
### WARNING ### Error trapped while processing command-line:
                Unknown option:

\end{verbatim}
% $
\end{minipage}\\\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{small}
\caption[Fixing {\tt{}GetOptions} for using '{\tt{}-}' as '{\tt{}STDIN}' mark.]{\label{tbl:STDINhandle} Errors reported when using '{\tt{}-}' as '{\tt{}STDIN}' mark and fixed width {\tt{}\LA{}looking for STDIN~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-looH-1}}\RA{}}.}
\end{center}
\end{table}

To avoid such errors, we capture the single dash when present in the command-line arguments list. 

'{\tt{}{\char36}cmdln{\char95}stdin}' will be used by '{\tt{}{\char38}set{\char95}input{\char95}file}' function to include the '{\tt{}STDIN}' in the correct ordering.\label{sec:stdinfix}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{33}\sublabel{NWgff18-looH-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-looH-1}}}\moddef{looking for STDIN~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-looH-1}}}\endmoddef
my $cmdln_stdin = undef;
for (my $a = 0; $a <= $#ARGV; $a++) \{ 
    next unless $ARGV[$a] =~ /^-$/o;
    $cmdln_stdin = $a - $#ARGV;
    splice(@ARGV,$a,1);
\};    
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-ParS-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{34}\nwdocspar

The following two code chunks define what to do if reports are sent to a file which is set in '{\tt{}{\char36}logs{\char95}filename}'.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{35}\sublabel{NWgff18-opeC-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-opeC-1}}}\moddef{open LOGFILE~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-opeC-1}}}\endmoddef
CHKLOG:
  (defined($logs_filename)) && do \{
      open(LOGFILE,"> ".$logs_filename) ||
          (&warn('FILE_NO_OPEN',$T,$logs_filename),last CHKLOG);
      $LogFile = 1;
  \};
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-ParS-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{36}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{37}\sublabel{NWgff18-ComF-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ComF-1}}}\moddef{Common Routines~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ComF-1}}}\endmoddef
sub close_logfile() \{ close(LOGFILE) if $LogFile \};
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-ComF-2}\\{NWgff18-ComF-3}\\{NWgff18-ComF-4}\\{NWgff18-ComF-5}\\{NWgff18-ComF-6}\\{NWgff18-ComF-7}\\{NWgff18-ComF-8}\\{NWgff18-ComF-9}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-APL5-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{38}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{39}\sublabel{NWgff18-UseB-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UseB-2}}}\moddef{Use Modules~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-UseB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
use Getopt::Long;
Getopt::Long::Configure qw/ bundling /;
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{40}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{41}\sublabel{NWgff18-perI-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-perI-2}}}\moddef{perl requires help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-perI-1}}}\plusendmoddef

my ($Debug,$Verbose,$Quiet,$LogFile,$logs_filename) = (0,0,0,0,undef);

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{45}\sublabel{NWgff18-ward-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ward-1}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ward-1}}}\endmoddef

  $Warn."Error trapped while processing command-line:\\n".(" "x16)."\\%s\\n",
CMD_LINE_ERROR =>

\subsubsctn{Special command-line options (forcing exit from program)}

The first command-line checking looks for those options exiting the program: '{\tt{}help}' and '{\tt{}version}'. Both need to output to screen without any other message/warning being displayed at the same time.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{47}\sublabel{NWgff18-comK-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}}\moddef{command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}}\endmoddef
"h|help|?"  => \\&prt_help,
"version"   => \\&prt_version, 
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-comK-2}\\{NWgff18-comK-3}\\{NWgff18-comK-4}\\{NWgff18-comK-5}\\{NWgff18-comK-6}\\{NWgff18-comK-7}\\{NWgff18-comK-8}\\{NWgff18-comK-9}\\{NWgff18-comK-A}\\{NWgff18-comK-B}\\{NWgff18-comK-C}\\{NWgff18-comK-D}\\{NWgff18-comK-E}\\{NWgff18-comK-F}\\{NWgff18-comK-G}\\{NWgff18-comK-H}\\{NWgff18-comK-I}\\{NWgff18-comK-J}\\{NWgff18-comK-K}\\{NWgff18-comK-L}\\{NWgff18-comK-M}\\{NWgff18-comK-N}\\{NWgff18-comK-O}\\{NWgff18-comK-P}\\{NWgff18-comK-Q}\\{NWgff18-comK-R}\\{NWgff18-comK-S}\\{NWgff18-comK-T}\\{NWgff18-comK-U}\\{NWgff18-comK-V}\\{NWgff18-comK-W}\\{NWgff18-comK-X}\\{NWgff18-comK-Y}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-ParS-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{48}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{49}\sublabel{NWgff18-comH-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-2}}}\moddef{command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}}\plusendmoddef
-h, --help    Shows this help.
--version     Shows current version and exits.
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{50}\nwdocspar
\begin{comment}
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{51}\sublabel{NWgff18-comO-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-1}}}\moddef{command-line latex short~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-1}}}\endmoddef

%<command-line latex>>=
%\clritem{-h{\x}-\/-help}
%\clritem{-\/-version}
%@
\end{comment}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{53}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParS-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-2}}}\moddef{Parsing Command-Line Options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub prt_version() \{
    my $comment = $MessageList\{'SHOW_VERSION'\};
    $comment = sprintf($comment,$PROGRAM,$VERSION);
    &prt_to_stderr($comment);
    exit(1);
\}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{54}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{55}\sublabel{NWgff18-mesd-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-mesd-1}}}\moddef{messages - parsing command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-mesd-1}}}\endmoddef
SHOW_VERSION =>
  $sp."### \\%s -- \\%s\\n".$sp,
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-H}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{56}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Testing command-line input filenames}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{57}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParS-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-3}}}\moddef{Parsing Command-Line Options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParS-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub set_input_file() \{
    my $stdin_flg = $F;
    \LA{}STDIN backwards compatibility~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-STDT-1}}\RA{}
    &report("CHECKING_FILENAMES");
  FILECHK: foreach my $test_file (@ARGV) \{
        $test_file ne '-' && do \{
            -e $test_file || do \{
                &warn('FILE_NO_OPEN',$T,$test_file);
                next FILECHK;
            \};
            &report('READING_FILE',$test_file);
            push @data_files, $test_file;
            next FILECHK;
        \};
        $stdin_flg = $T;
        push @data_files, '-';
    \}; # foreach
    scalar(@data_files) == 0 && do \{
        push @data_files, '-';
        $stdin_flg = $T;
    \};
    $stdin_flg && &report('READING_STDIN');
\}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{58}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{59}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-4}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my (@data_files,$file);
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{60}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{61}\sublabel{NWgff18-outN-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-outN-1}}}\moddef{warnings - input/output~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-outN-1}}}\endmoddef
FILE_NO_OPEN =>
  $spl.$Warn."Cannot Open Current file \\"\\%s\\" . Not used !!!\\n".$spl,
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-outN-2}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-G}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{62}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{63}\sublabel{NWgff18-outN.2-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-outN.2-1}}}\moddef{messages - input/output~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-outN.2-1}}}\endmoddef
CHECKING_FILENAMES =>
  $sp."### Validating INPUT FILENAMES\\n".$sp,
READING_FILE =>
  "###---> \\"\\%s\\" exists, including as Input File.\\n",
READING_STDIN =>
  "###---> Including GFF records from standard input.\\n",  
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-outN.2-2}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-H}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{64}\nwdocspar

Here is the fix for the explained in section~\ref{sec:stdinfix} on page~\pageref{sec:stdinfix} ({\tt{}\LA{}looking for STDIN~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-looH-1}}\RA{}} code).

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{65}\sublabel{NWgff18-STDT-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-STDT-1}}}\moddef{STDIN backwards compatibility~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-STDT-1}}}\endmoddef
my $chk_stdin = shift @_;
my $t = scalar(@ARGV);
defined($chk_stdin) && do \{
    abs($chk_stdin) > $t && ($chk_stdin = -$t);
    $chk_stdin > 0  && ($chk_stdin = 0 );
    $t += $chk_stdin;
    splice(@ARGV,$t,0,'-');
\};
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-ParS-3}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{66}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Verifying command-line settings}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{67}\sublabel{NWgff18-CheQ-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-CheQ-1}}}\moddef{Check command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-CheQ-1}}}\endmoddef
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-ParS-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{68}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Setting customization parameters from files} 

Here we define the command-line option for loading customization files.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{69}\sublabel{NWgff18-comR-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comR-1}}}\moddef{command-line options custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comR-1}}}\endmoddef
"O|custom-filename=s@"  => \\@custom_files,
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-comK-4}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{70}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{71}\sublabel{NWgff18-comO.2-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO.2-1}}}\moddef{command-line help custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO.2-1}}}\endmoddef
-O, --custom-filename <custom_filename> Load a configuration file 
         (if default \\".gff2aplotrc\\" exists is loaded before it).
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-comH-5}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{72}\nwdocspar
\begin{comment}
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{73}\sublabel{NWgff18-comV-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comV-1}}}\moddef{command-line latex short custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comV-1}}}\endmoddef
\\rw\{-O\{\\x\}-\\/-custom-filename \\pr\{file\}\}
  \{Read customization parameters from file.\}
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-comO-4}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{74}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{75}\sublabel{NWgff18-comP-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comP-1}}}\moddef{command-line latex custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comP-1}}}\endmoddef
\\clmitem\{-O \\pr\{custom\\_filename\}\\\\-\\/-custom-filename \\pr\{custom\\_filename\}\}
Loading customization parameters from '\\pr\{custom\\_file\}'. Now you can load several customization files by passing this option several times. The precedence is the input order in the command-line, so, for the common definitions, the last '\\pr\{custom\\_file\}' will override previous '\\pr\{custom\\_files\}' settings.
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-comI-3}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{76}\nwdocspar
\end{comment}

\subsubsctn{Testing whether custom-files exist}

Customization parameters cannot be set from '{\tt{}STDIN}'. What program does first of all, is to look whether default custom file does exist or not. But we are taking advantage of the fact that we also have to check existence of the command-line custom files (if given), so we insert as first element of the array the default custom file to the variable '{\tt{}@custom{\char95}files}' and then we check all its elements with the same function. We look for these files in current path and if they are not found in '{\tt{}{\char36}Custom{\char95}path}'.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{77}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParK-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-1}}}\moddef{Parsing Custom Files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-1}}}\endmoddef
sub set_custom_files() \{
    unshift @custom_files, $Custom_file;
    my @files = ();
    &report("CHECKING_CUSTOM_NAMES");
  MLOOP: foreach my $test_file (@custom_files) \{
      FILECHK: \{
        -e $test_file && last FILECHK;
        ($test_file =~ m\{/\}og || $Custom_path eq '.') || do \{
            my $tmpfl = $test_file;
            $test_file = "$Custom_path/$test_file";
            &report('READING_FROM_PATH',$tmpfl,$test_file);
            -e $test_file && last FILECHK;
        \};
        scalar(@custom_files) == 1 && do \{
            &report('NO_CUSTOM_FILES',$T);
            last MLOOP;
        \};
        &warn('FILE_NO_OPEN',$T,$test_file);
        next MLOOP;
      \}; # FILECHK
        &report('READING_CUSTOM_FILE',$test_file);
        push @files, $test_file;
    \}; # MLOOP: foreach
    @custom_files = @files;
\} # set_custom_files
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-ParK-2}\\{NWgff18-ParK-3}\\{NWgff18-ParK-4}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{78}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{79}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-5}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-5}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my @custom_files = ();
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{80}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{81}\sublabel{NWgff18-outN.2-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-outN.2-2}}}\moddef{messages - input/output~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-outN.2-1}}}\plusendmoddef
CHECKING_CUSTOM_NAMES =>
  $sp."### Validating CUSTOM FILENAMES\\n".$sp,
READING_FROM_PATH =>
  "###---> Custom File NOT FOUND in local path: \\"\\%s\\"\\n".
  "###     Trying to find in \\"GFF2APLOT_CUSTOMPATH\\": \\"\\%s\\"\\n",
READING_CUSTOM_FILE =>
  "###---> \\"\\%s\\" exists, including as Custom File.\\n",
NO_CUSTOM_FILES =>
  "###---> NO CUSTOM FILES found. Using program DEFAULTS.\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{82}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Parsing customization files}

Layout variables are defined as two fields, variable name and value, while the other variables require three fields, a feature to which is set the variable to the given value. To validate input records, '{\tt{}{\char36}var{\char95}flag}' boolean will determine whether a two fields or a three fields record we currently are going to process. '{\tt{}{\char38}varscheck}' function not only checks the customization parameters for correctness but also loads '{\tt{}{\char37}CustomVars}' hash.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{83}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParK-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-2}}}\moddef{Parsing Custom Files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub parse_custom_files() \{
    &header("READING CUSTOM FILES");
  MAIN: \{
      scalar(@custom_files) == 0 && do \{
          &report('NO_CUSTOM_FOUND',$file);
          last MAIN;
      \};
    LOAD: foreach $file (@custom_files) \{
        open(THIS,"< $file") ||
            ( &warn('FILE_NO_OPEN',$T,$file), next LOAD);
        &report('READ_CUSTOM_FILE',$file);
        ($n,$c) = (0,undef);
        while (<THIS>) \{
            my (@line,$main,$_c,$_v,$v_flag);
            /^\\#/o && do \{
                /^\\# ([LQSTGF]) \\#/o && do \{ 
                     $_c = $1; $c = '*';
                     $v_flag = ($_c ne 'L') ? $T : $F;
                     $_v = $varkeys\{$_c\};
                     next;
                \};
                $c = '.'; next;
            \};
            ($c = '.', next) if /^\\s*$/o;
            chomp;
            ($main,undef) = split /\\b\\s+\\#/o;
          TWOTHREE: \{
              $v_flag && do \{
                  $main =~ /^(.*?):\{2\}(.*?)=\{1\}(.*?)$/o &&
                      (@line = ($1,$2,$3));
                  last TWOTHREE;
              \};
              $main =~ /^(.*?)=\{1\}(.*?)$/o &&
                  (@line = ($_v,$1,$2));
          \}; # TWOTHREE
            $c = &varscheck($v_flag,$_v,\\@line) ? $_c : $noCV;
        \} continue \{
            &counter(++$n,$c) if ($Verbose && !$Quiet);
        \}; # WHILE
        &counter_end($n,$c) if ($Verbose && !$Quiet);
        close(THIS);
    \}; # LOAD
  \}; # MAIN
    print LOGFILE Dumper(\\%CustomVars) if ($LogFile && $Debug);
    &footer("CUSTOM FILES LOADED");
\} # parse_custom_files
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{84}\nwdocspar

\begin{table}[!t]
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{cc}
\fbox{
\begin{tabular}[b]{c>{\bfseries}c}
\textbf{Record TYPE} & \textbf{Symbol} \\
Empty record            & . \\
Comment                 & . \\
Header (\# [LQSTGF] \#) & * \\
Layout Vars             & L \\
Sequence Vars           & Q \\
Source Vars             & S \\
Strand Vars             & T \\
Group Vars              & G \\
Feature Vars            & F \\
Unknown                 & ? \\
\end{tabular}
} %fbox
&
\parbox[b]{0.4\linewidth}{
\caption[Symbols used to report record type from custom files]{\label{tbl:CFkeysXreport} Symbols used to report record type when parsing customization files (and {\tt{}STDERR} verbose mode is enabled with '{\tt{}-v}' switch).}
} % parbox
\\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{table}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{85}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloG-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-3}}}\moddef{Global Constants~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my $noCV = '?';
my %varkeys = (
    L => 'LAYOUT',
    Q => 'SEQUENCE',
    S => 'SOURCE',
    T => 'STRAND',
    G => 'GROUP',
    F => 'FEATURE',
    );
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{86}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{87}\sublabel{NWgff18-mesV-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-mesV-1}}}\moddef{messages - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-mesV-1}}}\endmoddef
READ_CUSTOM_FILE => 
  $sp."### Reading Customization Parameters from \\"\\%s\\"\\n".$sp,
NO_CUSTOM_FOUND =>
  $sp."### NO CUSTOM FILES found: Using program DEFAULTS.\\n".$sp,
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-H}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{88}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Validating customization parameters} 

'{\tt{}{\char36}rec}' is a reference to an array that contains three elements: feature, variable and value. First we check if variable name is defined in , then we check if the given value matches the variable type. After that we analyse the feature element, testing if it is a regular expression or not.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{89}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParK-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-3}}}\moddef{Parsing Custom Files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub varscheck() \{
    my ($flag,$class,$rec) = @_;
    defined($class) || 
        (&warn('SECTION_NOT_DEF',$F),return $F);
    my $_var = \\%\{$DefaultVars\{$class\}\};
    defined($_var->\{$$rec[1]\}) || 
        (&warn('VAR_NOT_DEFINED',$F,$class,$$rec[1]),return $F);
    &checkvarvalues($_var->\{$$rec[1]\}\{'TYPE'\},\\$$rec[2],$$rec[1]) || return $F;
#
# Regexp checking for $$rec[0] left 
#
    $flag && do \{
        push @\{$CustomVars\{$class\}\{$$rec[1]\}\}, [ $$rec[0], $$rec[2] ];
        return $T;
    \};
    $CustomVars\{$class\}\{$$rec[1]\} = $$rec[2];
    return $T;
\} # varscheck
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{90}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{91}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\endmoddef
SECTION_NOT_DEF =>
  $Warn."You probably forgot a section header, unable to parse this record.\\n",
VAR_NOT_DEFINED =>
  $Warn."\\%s variable not defined: \\"\\%s\\" .\\n",
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-warV-2}\\{NWgff18-warV-3}\\{NWgff18-warV-4}\\{NWgff18-warV-5}\\{NWgff18-warV-6}\\{NWgff18-warV-7}\\{NWgff18-warV-8}\\{NWgff18-warV-9}\\{NWgff18-warV-A}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-G}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{92}\nwdocspar

Different data requires different value tests, another function of those tests is to normalize when needed variable values to fixed internal values, so this will avoid later checkings or functions for reformating them and writing functions
will be simplest.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{93}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParK-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-4}}}\moddef{Parsing Custom Files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParK-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub checkvarvalues() \{
    my ($_test,$_val,$_var) = @_;
    my $_t = lc($$_val);
    \LA{}variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}\RA{}
    &warn('VARTYPE_NOT_DEFINED',$T,$_test,$_var);
    return $F;
\} # checkvarvalues
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{94}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{95}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-2}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
VARTYPE_NOT_DEFINED =>
  $Error."Variable type \\"\\%s\\" not defined,\\n".
  $spw."  could not check value for \\"\\%s\\".\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{96}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Customization variable values validation}

This section is dedicated to those test we need to ensure that customization variables contain acceptable values, so we do not need to check them later in the program. Table~\ref{tbl:varformats} summarizes the variable types defined for customization parameters.

\begin{table}[!t]
\begin{center}
\fbox{
\begin{tabular}{cl}
BOOLEAN  & A true/false variable.\\
STRING   & A free text character string.\\
DIGIT    & A natural number (nor decimals neither sign).\\
INTEGER  & Positive or negative integers.\\
DECIMAL  & Numbers with decimal values.\\
REALNUM  & Any number, including scientific notation.\\
COLOR    & Available colors are defined in '{\tt{}{\char37}COLORS}' hash.\\
PAGE     & Page sizes are set in '{\tt{}{\char37}FORMATS}' variable.\\
DNABASE  & A numeric value with nucleotide units (Gb, Mb, Kb or bases).\\
RANGE    & A 'lower-limit..upper-limit' numeric pair.\\
FONT     & A {\ps} from those defined in '{\tt{}{\char37}Fonts}' hash.\\
FONT\_SZ & A numeric value with font-size units (cm, mm, in or pt ---points---).\\
\end{tabular}
} % fbox
\caption[Customization parameters available formats]{\label{tbl:varformats} Parameter available formats we are going to use for customization variables checking.}
\end{center}
\end{table}

\subsubsctn{Checking boolean variables}

We define as 'BOOLEAN' those variables used as flags or switches, which can hold only a binary value such ON/OFF. Booleans are NOT case sensitive.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{97}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\endmoddef
$_test eq 'BOOLEAN' && do \{
    $_t =~ /^(1|on|t(rue)|y(es))$/o && ($$_val = $T, return $T);
    $_t =~ /^(0|off|f(alse)|n(o))$/o && ($$_val = $F, return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_BOOLEAN',$F,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-varN-2}\\{NWgff18-varN-3}\\{NWgff18-varN-4}\\{NWgff18-varN-5}\\{NWgff18-varN-6}\\{NWgff18-varN-7}\\{NWgff18-varN-8}\\{NWgff18-varN-9}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-ParK-4}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{98}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{99}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-3}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_BOOLEAN =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" variable requires a boolean value:\\n".
  $spw."     (ON/OFF, 1/0, TRUE/FALSE, YES/NO)\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{100}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Protecting reserved characters in strings}

Having a 'STRING' implies to replace/protect those characters that will produce indesirable effects in {\ps} code (such unbalanced parentheses). No error is reported for strings because they are assumed to be free text.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{101}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-2}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'STRING' && do \{
    $$_val =~ s\{[\\\\]\}\{\\\\134\}og;
    $$_val =~ s\{[\\(]\}\{\\\\050\}og;
    $$_val =~ s\{[\\)]\}\{\\\\051\}og;
    return $T;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{102}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Validating numbers}

The following tests look for four different number types.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{103}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-3}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'DIGIT' && do \{
    $$_val =~ /^\\d+$/o && (return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_DIGIT',$F,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
$_test eq 'INTEGER' && do \{
    $$_val =~ /^[+-]?\\d+$/o && (return $T);
    &warn('NOT_AN_INTEGER',$F,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
$_test eq 'DECIMAL' && do \{
    $$_val =~ /^[+-]?(?:\\d+(?:\\.\\d*)?|\\.\\d+)$/o && (return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_DECIMAL',$F,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
$_test eq 'REALNUM' && do \{
    $$_val =~ /^([+-]?)(?=\\d|\\.\\d)\\d*(\\.\\d*)?([Ee]([+-]?\\d+))?$/o &&
        (return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_REAL',$F,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{104}%$

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{105}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-4}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_DIGIT =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" variable requires a digit (natural number).\\n",
NOT_AN_INTEGER =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" variable requires an integer.\\n",
NOT_A_DECIMAL =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" variable requires a decimal number.\\n",
NOT_A_REAL =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" variable requires a real number (with exponent).\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{106}%$

\subsubsctn{Looking for color names}

Available colors are shown in section~\ref{sec:CMYKcolordef}, page~\pageref{sec:CMYKcolordef}. Here we check that customization input colors match those defined colors, including 'background' and 'foreground' colors. Color names are NOT case sensitive.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{107}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-4}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'COLOR' && do \{ # lc
    $_t =~ /^(b(ack)?|f(ore)?)g(round)?(color)?/o &&
        ($$_val = $_t, return $T);
    defined($COLORS\{$_t\}) && ($$_val = $_t, return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_COLOR',$F,$_t,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{108}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{109}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-5}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-5}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_COLOR =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" color not defined in \\"\\%s\\" variable.\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{110}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Verifying named page-sizes}

Available page sizes are shown in section~\ref{sec:PAGEdef}, page~\pageref{sec:PAGEdef}.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{111}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-5}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-5}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'PAGE' && do \{ # lc
    defined($FORMATS\{$_t\}) && ($$_val = $_t, return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_PAGE',$F,$_t,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{112}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{113}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-6}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-6}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_PAGE =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" page-size is not defined for \\"\\%s\\" variable.\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{114}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Nucleotide coords}

Those numbers relative to DNA positions may be given in bases, kilobases, megabases or gigabases, being last three ones a way to avoid any mistake when a big coord with lots of zeroes is provided. If no units are provided, then we asume bases.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{115}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-6}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-6}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'DNABASE' && do \{ # lc
    $_t =~ /^[+-]?(?:\\d+(?:\\.\\d*)?|\\.\\d+)([gmk]?b(ases)?)?$/o && 
        ($$_val = $_t, return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_DNABASE',$F,$_var,$_t);
    return $F;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{116}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{117}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-7}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-7}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_DNABASE =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" variable requires nucleotide units.\\n".
  $spw." \\"\\%s\\" is not valid (units must be in Gb, Mb, Kb, or bases).\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{118}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Accepting numeric ranges}

A range is a lower/upper limits pair for a given variable. One of the limits, or both, can be an asterisk ('*'), which means that the default value must be used.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{119}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-7}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-7}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'RANGE' && do \{

    return $T;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{120}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Checking for available fonts and font-sizes}

Font names must be in first capital letter format for {\ps}. 

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{121}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-8}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-8}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'FONT' && do \{ # lc
    defined($Fonts\{$_t\}) && 
        ($$_val = $Fonts\{$_t\}, return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_FONT',$F,$_t,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{122}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{123}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-8}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-8}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_FONT =>
  $Warn."Sorry, \\"\\%s\\" font is not defined for \\"\\%s\\" variable.\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{124}\nwdocspar

We provide three basic fonts that are standard in most {\ps} devices (a serif, a sans-serif and a monospaced font), and four series for each one (an upright ``normal'', an italic/oblique, a bold, and a bold italic/oblique series). 

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{125}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-6}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-6}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my %Fonts = (
    # serif
    times                   => 'Times-Roman',
    'times-roman'           => 'Times-Roman',
    'times-italic'          => 'Times-Italic',
    'times-bold'            => 'Times-Bold',
    'times-bolditalic'      => 'Times-BoldItalic',
    # sans serif
    helvetica               => 'Helvetica',
    'helvetica-oblique'     => 'Helvetica-Oblique',
    'helvetica-bold'        => 'Helvetica-Bold',
    'helvetica-boldoblique' => 'Helvetica-BoldOblique',
    # monospaced
    courier                 => 'Courier',
    'courier-oblique'       => 'Courier-Oblique',
    'courier-bold'          => 'Courier-Bold',
    'courier-boldoblique'   => 'Courier-BoldOblique',
    );
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{126}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{127}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-9}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-9}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_FONT =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" font is not available for \\"\\%s\\" variable.\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{128}\nwdocspar

Font sizes can be given in points, centimeters or inches. If no units are provided, then we asume points.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{129}\sublabel{NWgff18-varN-9}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-9}}}\moddef{variable value checking~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-varN-1}}}\plusendmoddef
$_test eq 'FONT_SZ' && do \{
    $_t =~ /^[+-]?(?:\\d+(?:\\.\\d*)?|\\.\\d+)
            (pt|cm|mm|in(ches)?|points|(centi|mili)meters)?$/ox && 
        ($$_val = $_t, return $T);
    &warn('NOT_A_FONTSIZE',$F,$_t,$_var);
    return $F;
\};
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{130}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{131}\sublabel{NWgff18-warV-A}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-A}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing custom files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warV-1}}}\plusendmoddef
NOT_A_FONTSIZE =>
  $Warn."\\"\\%s\\" is not a valid font-size for \\"\\%s\\" variable.",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{132}\nwdocspar

\sctn{Customization Variables Description} %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
    \label{sec:customvardesc}
% \subsctn{Command-line options}

Two options are used for reporting how program is running. By default no messages are shown to standard error, only errors. One reports to a log file defined by user and the other shows the messages to standard error, both can be activated at the same time. A third one is needed to disable STDERR warnings.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{133}\sublabel{NWgff18-comK-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-2}}}\moddef{command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}}\plusendmoddef
"v|verbose"   => \\$Verbose, # Print_Report
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{134}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{135}\sublabel{NWgff18-comH-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-3}}}\moddef{command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}}\plusendmoddef
-v, --verbose    Verbose mode, a full report is sent to standard error 
                 (default is set to showing only WARNINGS).
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{136}\nwdocspar
\begin{comment}
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{137}\sublabel{NWgff18-comO-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-2}}}\moddef{command-line latex short~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-1}}}\plusendmoddef
\\rw\{-v\{\\x\}-\\/-verbose\}
  \{Verbose mode, a full report is sent to standard error.\}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{138}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{139}\sublabel{NWgff18-comI-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comI-1}}}\moddef{command-line latex~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comI-1}}}\endmoddef
\\clmitem\{-v\\\\-\\/-verbose\}
By default, warnings and errors are sent to standard error. This option 
switches on process reporting messages to appear on standard error too.
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-comI-2}\\{NWgff18-comI-3}\\{NWgff18-comI-4}\\{NWgff18-comI-5}\\{NWgff18-comI-6}\\{NWgff18-comI-7}\\{NWgff18-comI-8}\\{NWgff18-comI-9}\\{NWgff18-comI-A}\\{NWgff18-comI-B}\\{NWgff18-comI-C}\\{NWgff18-comI-D}\\{NWgff18-comI-E}\\{NWgff18-comI-F}\\{NWgff18-comI-G}\\{NWgff18-comI-H}\\{NWgff18-comI-I}\\{NWgff18-comI-J}\\{NWgff18-comI-K}\\{NWgff18-comI-L}\\{NWgff18-comI-M}\\{NWgff18-comI-N}\\{NWgff18-comI-O}\\{NWgff18-comI-P}\\{NWgff18-comI-Q}\\{NWgff18-comI-R}\\{NWgff18-comI-S}\\{NWgff18-comI-T}\\{NWgff18-comI-U}\\{NWgff18-comI-V}\\{NWgff18-comI-W}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-LATI-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{140}\nwdocspar
\end{comment}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{141}\sublabel{NWgff18-comK-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-3}}}\moddef{command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}}\plusendmoddef
"V|logs-filename=s"  => \\$logs_filename, # Print_Report -> LogFile
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{142}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{143}\sublabel{NWgff18-comH-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-4}}}\moddef{command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}}\plusendmoddef
-V, --logs-filename <logs_filename>    Report is written to a log file.
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{144}\nwdocspar
\begin{comment}
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{145}\sublabel{NWgff18-comO-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-3}}}\moddef{command-line latex short~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-1}}}\plusendmoddef
\\rw\{-V\{\\x\}-\\/-logs-filename \\pr\{file\}\}
  \{Report is written to a log file.\}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{146}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{147}\sublabel{NWgff18-comI-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comI-2}}}\moddef{command-line latex~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
\\clmitem\{-V \\pr\{logs\\_filename\}\\\\-\\/-logs-filename \\pr\{logs\\_filename\}\}
If is possible to open '\\pr\{logs\\_filename\}' then such file will contain 
all the messages and warnings produced by the program even though they 
will be disabled from standard error with \\tp\{-\\/-quiet\} option.
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{148}\nwdocspar
\end{comment}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{149}\sublabel{NWgff18-comK-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-4}}}\moddef{command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}}\plusendmoddef
"q|quiet"   => \\$Quiet, # Quiet_Mode
\LA{}command-line options custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comR-1}}\RA{}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{150}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{151}\sublabel{NWgff18-comH-5}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-5}}}\moddef{command-line help~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comH-1}}}\plusendmoddef
-q, --quiet    Quiet mode, do not show any message/warning
               to standard error (only ERRORS are reported).
\LA{}command-line help custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO.2-1}}\RA{}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{152}\nwdocspar
\begin{comment}
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{153}\sublabel{NWgff18-comO-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-4}}}\moddef{command-line latex short~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comO-1}}}\plusendmoddef
\\rw\{-q\{\\x\}-\\/-quiet\}
  \{Quiet mode, messages/warnings disabled (only ERRORS are reported)\}
\LA{}command-line latex short custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comV-1}}\RA{}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{154}\nwdocspar
\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{155}\sublabel{NWgff18-comI-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comI-3}}}\moddef{command-line latex~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
\\clmitem\{-q\\\\-\\/-quiet\}
This option disables any message or warning from standard error. It does not 
disable error report because such errors are pointing a problem which can 
make \{\\prog\} produce unexpected results. Solve the cause of such problems 
before continuing to run the program in a silent mode. 
\LA{}command-line latex custom~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comP-1}}\RA{}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{156}\nwdocspar
\end{comment}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{157}\sublabel{NWgff18-comK-5}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-5}}}\moddef{command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-comK-1}}}\plusendmoddef

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{389}\sublabel{NWgff18-ChaV-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ChaV-1}}}\moddef{Changes in command-line options~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ChaV-1}}}\endmoddef
# "i"  => # Page_Orientation
# "F"  => \\$CmdLineVars\{""\}, # Function_COLOR;Display_FUNCTION;Display_EXTRA-BOX
# "f"  => \\$CmdLineVars\{""\}, # Display_FUNCTION; Display_EXTRA-BOX
# "M"  => \\$CmdLineVars\{""\}, # Display_GFF; Display_EXTRA-BOX
# "m"  => \\$CmdLineVars\{""\}, # Display_GFF-ReverseOrder; Display_EXTRA-BOX
\nwnotused{Changes\ in\ command-line\ options}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{390}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{391}\sublabel{NWgff18-defQ-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defQ-1}}}\moddef{default layout vars values~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-defQ-1}}}\endmoddef
#                         
page_size                  => \{ TYPE => 'PAGE'   , VALUE => 'a4'   \},
background_color           => \{ TYPE => 'COLOR'  , VALUE => 'white' \},
foreground_color           => \{ TYPE => 'COLOR'  , VALUE => 'black' \},
# GLOBAL Labels           
show_title                 => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
title                      => \{ TYPE => 'STRING' , VALUE => undef  \},
show_subtitle              => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
subtitle                   => \{ TYPE => 'STRING' , VALUE => undef  \},
show_x_sequence_label      => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
x_sequence_label           => \{ TYPE => 'STRING' , VALUE => undef  \},
show_y_sequence_label      => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
x_sequence_label           => \{ TYPE => 'STRING' , VALUE => undef  \},
# TICKMARK features                                              
show_tickmark_label        => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_aplot_x_ticks         => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_percent_x_ticks       => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_extrabox_x_ticks      => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_aplot_y_ticks         => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_percent_y_ticks       => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_extrabox_y_ticks      => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $T     \},
show_onlylower_x_ticks     => \{ TYPE => 'BOOLEAN', VALUE => $F     \},
aplot_major_tickmark       => \{ TYPE => 'INTEGER', VALUE => 2      \},
aplot_minor_tickmark       => \{ TYPE => 'INTEGER', VALUE => 5      \},
percent_major_tickmark     => \{ TYPE => 'INTEGER', VALUE => 5      \},
percent_minor_tickmark     => \{ TYPE => 'INTEGER', VALUE => 5      \},
extra_major_tickmark       => \{ TYPE => 'INTEGER', VALUE => 2      \},
extra_minor_tickmark       => \{ TYPE => 'INTEGER', VALUE => 5      \},
major_tickmark_nucleotide  => \{ TYPE => 'DNABASE', VALUE => undef  \},
minor_tickmark_nucleotide  => \{ TYPE => 'DNABASE', VALUE => undef  \},

\sctn{Reading GFF records} %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

We have to deal with two basic formats, the \textsl{standard} General Feature Format (GFF) and the derived \textsl{aplot} format, the former having two versions with some minor differences at field level. We are going to asume the record formats shown in the table~\ref{fig:formats} for the input files.


\begin{table}[!t]
% \newcommand{\m}[1]{\multicolumn{2}{@{}c@{}}{#1}}
\begin{center}\setlength{\fboxsep}{10pt}
\fbox{
\begin{minipage}[c]{0.95\linewidth}
\begin{center}
\footnotesize
\textbf{\normalsize Record Format}\\[1ex]
\pa{seqname} \pa{source} \pa{feature} \pa{start} \pa{end} \pa{score} \pa{strand} \pa{frame} [attributes] [comments]\\[2ex]
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.5}\begin{tabular}{ccc}
\textbf{Field Name} & \textbf{GFF Version 1/Version 2} & \textbf{Aplot format} \\
\pa{seqname} & {\tt{}\ [{\char94}{\char92}{\char35}\ ]+\ }     & \pa{seqname1}:\pa{seqname2} \\
\pa{source}  & {\tt{}\ [{\char94}{\char92}{\char35}\ ]+\ }     & \pa{source}[:\pa{source}]   \\
\pa{feature} & {\tt{}\ [{\char94}{\char92}{\char35}\ ]+\ }     & \pa{feature}[:\pa{feature}] \\
\pa{start}   & {\tt{}\ [+-]?[0-9]+\ } & \pa{start1}:\pa{start2}     \\
\pa{end}     & {\tt{}\ [+-]?[0-9]+\ } & \pa{end1}:\pa{end2}         \\
\pa{score}   & {\tt{}\ [+-]?[0-9]*[.]?[0-9]*(e[+-]?[0-9]+)?\ } & \pa{alignment\_score}       \\[-1.5ex]
  (no score) & GFFv1 {\tt{}=>\ 0} / GFFv2 {\tt{}=>\ .} & . \\
\pa{strand}  & {\tt{}\ [+-.]\ }  & \pa{strand1}[:\pa{strand2}] \\
\pa{frame}   & {\tt{}\ [.012]\ } & \pa{frame1}[:\pa{frame2}]   \\[0.5ex]
\textbf{Field Separator} & GFFv1 {\tt{}=>\ {\char92}s+\ } / GFFv2 {\tt{}=>\ [{\char92}t]+\ } & {\tt{}\ {\char92}s+\ } \\
\end{tabular}\\[4ex]
\textbf{\normalsize Grouping fields}\\[1ex]
\begin{tabular}{rl}
 \,[attributes]  & \hspace{0.25cm}(\textsl{GFF v1\&v2, APLOT})\\
                 & group\_name [extra\_data]\\
                 & "group\_name" [extra\_data]\\
                 & \pa{tag} "group\_name" [extra\_data]\\[1ex]
 \,[extra\_data] & \\
                 & [\,[\pa{start2} \pa{end2} [\pa{strand2}] [\pa{frame2}]\,]; \pa{tag} \pa{value} [ \ldots ; \pa{tag} \pa{value}]\,]\\[2ex]
 \,[attributes]  & \hspace{0.25cm}(\textsl{APLOT old format})\\
                 & group\_name:element\_name [extra\_data]\\[1ex]
 \,[extra\_data] & \hspace{0.25cm}(\textsl{APLOT old format})\\
                 & [\,; \pa{tag} \pa{value} [ \ldots [ ; \pa{tag} \pa{value}]\,]\,]\\
\end{tabular}\\[4ex]
\textbf{\normalsize Other definitions}\\[1ex]
\begin{tabular}{rl}
 \,[comments]    & {\tt{}{\char35}\ Whatever\ extra\ information\ about\ this\ record...} \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{minipage}
} %fbox
\caption{\label{tbl:formats} Input records format definition for {\prog}.}
\end{center}
\end{table}


Function '{\tt{}{\char38}parse{\char95}GFF{\char95}files}' is only a wrapper for reporting the parsing process over GFF records. The main function call is '{\tt{}{\char38}fieldscheck}',which processes each GFF record and loads the values in its fields to the corresponding data structure. Although that, the wrapper checks if there are enough fields (8 required at least) and removes also any comment from the input record, assuming that a white space or a tab followed by a '{\tt{}{\char35}}' (as shown in this regular expression: '{\tt{}\ /{\char92}s+{\char92}{\char35}/\ }') is a comment mark, from there to the end of line everything is ignored.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{409}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\endmoddef
sub parse_GFF_files() \{
    &header("PARSING INPUT GFF RECORDS");
  LOAD: foreach $file (@data_files) \{
      open(THIS,"< $file") ||
          (&warn('FILE_NO_OPEN',$T,$file), next LOAD);
      $file eq '-' && ($file = 'STANDARD INPUT');
      &report('READ_GFF_FILE',$file);
      ($n,$c) = (0,undef);
      while (<THIS>) \{
          my (@line,$main);
          ($c = '.', next) if /^\\#/o;
          ($c = '.', next) if /^\\s*$/o;
          chomp;
          # $c = $noGFF;
          ($main,undef) = split /\\s+\\#/o;
          @line = split /\\s+/o, $main, 9;        
          scalar(@line) < 8 &&
              (&warn('NOT_ENOUGH_FIELDS',$F,$file,$n,join(" ",@line)), next);
          $c = &GFF_format(&fieldscheck(\\@line));
      \} continue \{
          &counter(++$n,$c) if ($Verbose && !$Quiet);
      \}; # WHILE
      &counter_end($n,$c) if ($Verbose && !$Quiet);
      close(THIS);
  \}; # LOAD
    print LOGFILE Dumper(\\%GFF_DATA) if ($LogFile && $Debug);
    &footer("DATA LOADED");
\} # sub parse_GFF
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-ParI-2}\\{NWgff18-ParI-3}\\{NWgff18-ParI-4}\\{NWgff18-ParI-5}\\{NWgff18-ParI-6}\\{NWgff18-ParI-7}\\{NWgff18-ParI-8}\\{NWgff18-ParI-9}\\{NWgff18-ParI-A}\\{NWgff18-ParI-B}\\{NWgff18-ParI-C}\\{NWgff18-ParI-D}\\{NWgff18-ParI-E}\\{NWgff18-ParI-F}\\{NWgff18-ParI-G}\\{NWgff18-ParI-H}\\{NWgff18-ParI-I}\\{NWgff18-ParI-J}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-MaiD-1}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{410}%$

We define the following constants, used to report which format was found in the current read record (See table~\ref{tbl:DTkeysXreport}).

\begin{table}[!t]
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{cc}
\fbox{
\begin{tabular}[b]{c>{\bfseries}c}
\textbf{Record TYPE} & \textbf{Symbol} \\
Empty record        & . \\
Comment             & . \\
GFF (grouped)       & X \\
GFF (ungrouped)     & x \\
GFF (alignment)     & A \\
GFF (vector)        & V \\
APLOT (grouped)     & O \\
APLOT (ungrouped)   & o \\
Unknown             & ? \\
\end{tabular}
} %fbox
&
\parbox[b]{0.4\linewidth}{
\caption[Symbols used to report record type from data files]{\label{tbl:DTkeysXreport} Symbols used to report record type when parsing input GFF files (and {\tt{}STDERR} verbose mode is enabled with '{\tt{}-v}' switch).}
} % parbox
\\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{table}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{411}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloG-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-4}}}\moddef{Global Constants~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloG-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my ($GFF,$GFF_NOGP,$VECTOR,$ALIGN,
    $APLOT,$APLOT_NOGP,$noGFF) =
    qw/ X x V A O o ? /;
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{412}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{413}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-7}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-7}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my ($n,$c);
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{414}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{415}\sublabel{NWgff18-warS-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-1}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing GFF files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-1}}}\endmoddef
NOT_ENOUGH_FIELDS =>
  $Warn."Not enough fields in file \\"\\%s\\", line \\%s :\\n\\t\\%s\\n",
\nwalsodefined{\\{NWgff18-warS-2}\\{NWgff18-warS-3}\\{NWgff18-warS-4}}\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-G}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{416}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{417}\sublabel{NWgff18-mesS-1}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-mesS-1}}}\moddef{messages - parsing GFF files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-mesS-1}}}\endmoddef
READ_GFF_FILE => 
  $sp."### Reading GFF records from \\"\\%s\\"\\n".$sp,
\nwused{\\{NWgff18-GloB-H}}\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{418}\nwdocspar

We set the character being printed in the parsing status output.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{419}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-2}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub GFF_format() \{
    my $gff = $_[0];
    # return "x" if $GFF == $version1;
    return $GFF        if $gff eq $GFF;        # $version2
    return $GFF_NOGP   if $gff eq $GFF_NOGP;   # $version2 (ungrouped)
    return $VECTOR     if $gff eq $VECTOR;     # VECTOR: GFFv2 particular case 
    return $ALIGN      if $gff eq $ALIGN;      # ALIGN: GFFv2 particular case
    return $APLOT      if $gff eq $APLOT;      # Old aplot format (with colons)
    return $APLOT_NOGP if $gff eq $APLOT_NOGP; # Old aplot format (ungrouped)
    return $noGFF;
\} # GFF_format
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{420}\nwdocspar

Here we decide to parse records as they are in GFF or in APLOT format. '{\tt{}load{\char95}gff}' and '{\tt{}load{\char95}aplot}' do the field error checking and load the program variables '{\tt{}{\char37}gff{\char95}data}' and '{\tt{}{\char37}aplot{\char95}data}'. Those variables are reset in '{\tt{}\LA{}Main Loop~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-Mai9-1}}\RA{}}'.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{421}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-3}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub fieldscheck() \{
    my ($list) = @_;
    my ($seqname,$start,$end) = @$list[0,3,4]; # ($list->[0],$list->[3],$list->[4]);
    (&fcolon($seqname) && &fcolon($start) && &fcolon($end)) && do \{
        return &load_aplot(\\@$list);
    \};
    return &load_gff(\\@$list);
\} # fieldscheck
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{422}\nwdocspar

For historical reasons the program can work with APLOT format (see Table~\ref{tbl:formats}). Initial field checking determines whether the record being processed is under that alignment GFF-like format, by determining that first, fourth and fifth fields contain a colon char. Then we assume we are under APLOT format.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{423}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-4}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub fcolon() \{ return ($_[0] =~ /.+:.+/o ? $T : $F) \}
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{424}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Validating fields}

The following functions checks whether some of the input GFF fields are well defined. They return '{\tt{}True}' ('{\tt{}{\char36}T}') if no error found and '{\tt{}False}' ('{\tt{}{\char36}F}') when input fields are wrong. The returned value forces '{\tt{}{\char38}load{\char95}aplot}' or '{\tt{}{\char38}load{\char95}gff}' functions to skip the records having format errors.

Here we test that '\pa{start}' field must be lower or equal than '\pa{end}':

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{425}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-5}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-5}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub check_coords() \{ # ((ori,end)_1,...,(ori,end)_n)
    my @ary = @_;
    for (my $j=0; $j<=$#ary; $j+=2) \{
        $ary[$j] > $ary[$j+1] && do \{
            &warn('ORI_GREATER_END',$F,$ary[$j],$ary[$j+1],$file,$n+1);
            return $F;
        \};
    \}; # foreach
    return $T;
\} # check_coords
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{426}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{427}\sublabel{NWgff18-warS-2}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-2}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing GFF files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-1}}}\plusendmoddef
ORI_GREATER_END =>
  $Warn."Start greater than end \\"\\%s > \\%s\\" in file \\"\\%s\\" line \\"\\%s\\".\\n", 
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{428}\nwdocspar

'\pa{strand}' field must contain only '+', '-' or '.' (for records having no strand).

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{429}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-6}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-6}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub check_strand() \{ # (str_1,...,srt_n)
    foreach my $str (@_) \{
        $str !~ /[+-.]/o && do \{
            &warn('STRAND_MISMATCH',$F,$str,$file,$n+1);
            return $F;
        \};
    \}; # foreach
    return $T;
\} # check_strand
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{430}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{431}\sublabel{NWgff18-warS-3}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-3}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing GFF files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-1}}}\plusendmoddef
STRAND_MISMATCH =>
  $Warn." Strand mismatch definition \\"\\%s\\" in file \\"\\%s\\" line \\"\\%s\\".\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{432}\nwdocspar

Same happens to '\pa{frame}', which only '0', '1', '2' or '.' (for those records having no frame) values are allowed.

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{433}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-7}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-7}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub check_frame() \{ # (frm_1,...,frm_n)
    foreach my $frm (@_) \{
        $frm !~ /[.012]/o && do \{
            &warn('FRAME_MISMATCH',$F,$frm,$file,$n+1);
            return $F;
        \};
    \}; # foreach
    return $T;
\} # check_frame
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{434}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{435}\sublabel{NWgff18-warS-4}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-4}}}\moddef{warnings - parsing GFF files~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-warS-1}}}\plusendmoddef
FRAME_MISMATCH =>
  $Warn." Frame mismatch definition \\"\\%s\\" in file \\"\\%s\\" line \\"\\%s\\".\\n",
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{436}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Parsing APLOT format}\label{sec:parseAPLOT}

'{\tt{}{\char38}check{\char95}aplot{\char95}fields}' will call to the '{\tt{}{\char38}add{\char95}aplot{\char95}record}' which loads the new record if everything is OK into '{\tt{}{\char37}ALN{\char95}DATA}' (see section~\ref{sec:APLOT-DS}). The first parameter for '{\tt{}{\char38}load{\char95}grouping}' function is set to 'False' is for APLOT grouping definition ('True' for GFF grouping definition, see section~\ref{sec:parseGFF}).

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{437}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-8}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-8}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub load_aplot() \{ # if errors found > return $noGFF
    my ($list) = @_;
    my $w_gff;
    ($seqname_1,$seqname_2,$source_1,$source_2,$feature_1,$feature_2,
     $start_1,$start_2,$end_1,$end_2,$score_1,$score_2,
     $strand_1,$strand_2,$frame_1,$frame_2) = 
     &remove_colon(@$list[0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7]);
    $w_gff = &load_grouping($F,$list->[8]);
    &check_aplot_fields || ($w_gff=$noGFF);
    return $w_gff;
\} # load_aplot
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{438}%$

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{439}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-8}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-8}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my ($seqname_1,$seqname_2,
    $source_1,$source_2,$feature_1,$feature_2,
    $start_1,$start_2,$end_1,$end_2,$score_1,$score_2,
    $strand_1,$strand_2,$frame_1,$frame_2); # APLOT temporary vars
my ($tag,$group,$group_id,$label,
    $group_gff_counter,$group_aplot_counter); # GROUPING temporary vars
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{440}\nwdocspar

\begin{table}[!t]
\begin{center}
\fbox{
\begin{tabular}{c@{\qquad}c}
Strand
\(
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\left\{
\begin{array}{c@{\quad\Rightarrow\quad}c}
\mbox{{\tt{}+}} & \mbox{{\tt{}+:+}}\\
\mbox{{\tt{}-}} & \mbox{{\tt{}-:-}}\\
\mbox{{\tt{}.}} & \mbox{{\tt{}.:.}}\\
\end{array}
\right.
\)
 &
Frame
\(
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\left\{
\begin{array}{c@{\quad\Rightarrow\quad}c}
\mbox{{\tt{}2}} & \mbox{{\tt{}2:2}}\\
\mbox{{\tt{}1}} & \mbox{{\tt{}1:1}}\\
\mbox{{\tt{}0}} & \mbox{{\tt{}0:0}}\\
\mbox{{\tt{}.}} & \mbox{{\tt{}.:.}}\\
\end{array}
\right.
\)
 \\
\end{tabular}
} % fbox
\parbox{0.75\linewidth}{
\caption[Retrieving second element when missing in old APLOT format]{\label{tbl:missingfields} For {\prog} old format, when in a '\pa{element1}:\pa{element2}' field pair the second element is missing, second is set to first element.}
} % parbox
\end{center}
\end{table}

When checking for colons, we assume that any element defined without colons is equal to the same value repeated twice (see Table~\ref{tbl:missingfields}). 

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{441}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-9}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-9}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub remove_colon() \{
    my @ary_out = ();
    my ($a,$b) = (undef,undef);
    foreach my $fld (@_) \{
        ($a,$b) = split /:/o, $fld, 2;
        $a = '.' unless defined($a);
        $b = $a  unless defined($b);
        push @ary_out, $a, $b;
    \};
    return @ary_out;
\} # remove_colon
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{442}%$

\subsubsctn{Checking fields and accepting APLOT records}

If records are OK, then we can append a new record to the variable defined for APLOT records (so called later in this section as '{\tt{}{\char37}ALN{\char95}DATA}').

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{443}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-A}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-A}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub check_aplot_fields() \{
    &check_coords($start_1,$end_1,$start_2,$end_2) || (return $F);
    &check_strand($strand_1,$strand_2) || (return $F);
    &check_frame($frame_1,$frame_2) || (return $F);
    &add_aplot_record;
    return $T; 
\} # check_aplot_fields
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{444}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{445}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-B}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-B}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub add_aplot_record() \{
    return;
\} # add_aplot_record
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{446}%$

\label{sec:APLOT-DS}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{447}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-9}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-9}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my (%ALN_DATA);
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{448}\nwdocspar

\subsctn{Parsing standard GFF format}\label{sec:parseGFF}

'{\tt{}{\char38}check{\char95}gff{\char95}fields}' will call to the '{\tt{}{\char38}add{\char95}gff{\char95}record}' which loads the new record if everything is OK into '{\tt{}{\char37}GFF{\char95}DATA}' (see section~\ref{sec:GFF-DS}). The first parameter for '{\tt{}{\char38}load{\char95}grouping}' function is set to 'True' for GFF grouping definition ('False' is for APLOT grouping definition, see section~\ref{sec:parseAPLOT}). 

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{449}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-C}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-C}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub load_gff() \{ # if errors found > return $noGFF
    my ($list) = @_ ;
    my $w_gff;
    ($seqname,$source,$feature,$start,$end,
     $score,$strand,$frame) = @$list[0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7];
    $w_gff = &load_grouping($T,$list->[8]);
    &check_gff_fields($w_gff) || ($w_gff=$noGFF);
    return $w_gff;
\} # load_gff
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{450}\nwdocspar

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{451}\sublabel{NWgff18-GloB-A}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-A}}}\moddef{Global Vars~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-GloB-1}}}\plusendmoddef
my ($seqname,$source,$feature,$start,
    $end,$score,$strand,$frame); # GFF temporary vars
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{452}\nwdocspar

\subsubsctn{Checking fields and accepting GFF records}

\nwenddocs{}\nwbegincode{453}\sublabel{NWgff18-ParI-D}\nwmargintag{{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-D}}}\moddef{Parsing Input Data~{\nwtagstyle{}\subpageref{NWgff18-ParI-1}}}\plusendmoddef
sub check_gff_fields() \{
    &check_coords($start,$end) || (return $F);
    &check_strand($strand) || (return $F);
    &check_frame($frame) || (return $F);
    &add_gff_record($_[0]);
    return $T; 
\} # check_gff_fields
\nwendcode{}\nwbegindocs{454}\nwdocspar

Once fields checking is done, we proceed to load the data structure defined for the GFF records as '{\tt{}{\char37}GFF{\char95}DATA}' hash.
The outline of the inner structure of that variable is shown in table~\ref{tbl:gffdata}.

\begin{table}[!ht]
\begin{center}
\input tables/DataStructure_GFF.tex
\caption[GFF internal data structure for {\prog}]{\label{tbl:gffdata} GFF internal data structure for {\prog}. The topmost hash corresponds to '{\tt{}{\char37}GFF{\char95}DATA}', the others are anonymous lists/hashes expanding from it.}
\end{center}
\end{table}

\begin{comment}%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

   \\end\{array\} \\right] $
